        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered to be a promising low-cost alternative to common lithium-ion batteries.  Herein, we present a detailed electrochem. characterization of anatase TiO2 nanoparticles as anode material for Na-ion batteries, highlighting the substantial influence of the electrolyte compn. (salt and solvent) on the obtainable specific capacity, cycling stability, and particularly the coulombic efficiency.  TiO2-based electrodes cycled using a 1M soln. of NaClO4 in a mixt. of ethylene carbonate and propylene carbonate present excellent high rate capability, offering about 100 and 86 mAh g-1 at 5.5 and 11 C, resp., which is - to the best of our knowledge - the best high rate capability for all titanium-based sodium-ion anode materials reported so far.  Setting the C rate to 5.5C (i.e., 1.85 A g-1), such electrodes can be cycled for more than 1000 cycles without significant capacity decay, confirming their outstanding durability at such high specific current.  These results, in combination with its environmental friendliness and cost efficiency, render anatase TiO2 nanoparticles a promising anode material for high power sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref29" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA00614G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jia, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Anatase TiO<sub>2</sub> Nanocubes for Fast and Durable Sodium Ion Battery Anodes</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anatase TiO2 nanocubes for fast and durable sodium ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Xuming; Wang, Chao; Yang, Yingchang; Zhang, Yan; Jia, Xinnan; Chen, Jun; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">With the aim of advancing anatase TiO2 anodes for Na ion batteries, cryst. TiO2 nanocubes were employed and they delivered a gradually increasing capacity during the initial cycles, termed as an activation process.  The no. of necessary discharge-charge loops for total activation is dependent on the galvanostatic c.d. (∼20 cycles at 0.2 C, or 90 cycles at 1 C).  A percentage of Ti3+ was detected after the activation, indicating an amt. of irreversibly trapped Na ions in the lattice. The capacity was sustained with a loss of &lt;10% after 1000 discharge-charge cycles at a rate of 2 C or 10 C.  The superior battery performance achieved by the nanocubes is related to the encircled {100} facets that are more favorable for Na ion attachment compared to the {001} and {101} facets, as supported by 1st-principles calcns.  From this work the authors can see the feasibility of optimizing electrode materials via rational surface structure construction based on theor. calcns.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref30" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1039/C5CP01227A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hou, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jing, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An Electrochemical Investigation of Rutile TiO<sub>2</sub> Microspheres Anchored by Nanoneedle Clusters for Sodium Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Phys.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Exploring new anode materials is important for developing sodium ion batteries.  In this work, TiO2(B) nanotubes are prepd. by hydrothermal reaction in concd. NaOH soln. and subsequent calcination at 300 °C in air, and investigated for the first time as anodes for sodium ion batteries.  It is demonstrated that TiO2(B) nanotubes are several hundred nanometers in length with an outer diam. of about 10-15 nm.  Moreover, the interference fringe spacings of the nanotubes are derived from the TEM image, being about 0.56 and 0.34 nm, which are consistent with the interplanar distances of the (001) and (110) planes in the TiO2(B) phase, resp. Meanwhile, the tubular morphol. can ensure the good high rate capability and cycle stability.  Therefore, TiO2(B) nanotubes present feasible electrochem. sodium storage, offering possibilities to develop new anode materials for sodium ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref34" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1039/C3TA13394J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Perez-Flores, J.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hollandite-type TiO2: a new negative electrode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Perez-Flores, J. C.; Baehtz, C.; Kuhn, A.; Garcia-Alvarado, F.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1825-1833</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. properties of TiO2 with the hollandite structure (TiO2(H)) as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries are reported.  TiO2(H) was obtained from hollandite K0.21TiO2 by an oxidn.-ion extn. process.  Na/TiO2(H) cells exhibit a large first discharge capacity of 280 mA-h/g down to 0.2 V.  After the first discharge the Na/TiO2(H) cells develop a reversible charge-discharge capacity of 85 mA-h/g at C/8 rate in the 2.5-0.2 V voltage range; this corresponds to the reversible insertion of 0.25 Na per TiO2(H) formula unit.  Chronoamperometry and potentiostatic intermittent titrn. techniques were used to further characterize the electrochem. reaction mechanism.  Structural changes in the TiO2(H) electrode upon sodium insertion and extn. have been studied by ex situ x-ray diffraction (XRD) and high resoln. in situ synchrotron diffraction techniques, for which appropriately modified coin-type cells were used.  It is seen that sodium insertion into TiO2(H) is commenced with a single-phase solid soln. followed by a structural transition from tetragonal I4/m to monoclinic I2/m symmetry, in which the skeleton framework is retained.  The reversible transition includes few structural changes with a small vol. change of only 1.1%.  Fourier difference maps deduced from SXRD patterns revealed the location of Na ions in 4i sites in the tunnel space.  The coordination arrangement around Na ions is distorted capped trigonal prisms formed by seven oxygen atoms. The electrochem. properties of the amorphous TiO2 nanospheres and the TiO2 hollow nanospheres with different phases were characterized as anodes for the Na-ion batteries.  It was found that all the samples demonstrated excellent cyclability, which was sustainable for hundreds of cycles with little capacity fading, although the anatase TiO2 presented a capability that was better than that of the mixed anatase/rutile TiO2 or the amorphous TiO2@C.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Polymn.-induced phase sepn. of nanoparticle-filled soln. is demonstrated as a simple approach to control the structure of porous composites.  These composites are subsequently demonstrated as the active component for sodium-ion battery anode.  To synthesize the composites, we dissolved/dispersed titanium oxide (anatase) nanoparticles (for sodium insertion) and poly(hydroxybutyl methacrylate) (porogen) in furfuryl alc. (carbon precursor) contg. a photoacid generator.  UV exposure converts the photoacid generator to a strong acid that catalyzes the furfuryl alc. polymn.  This polymn. simultaneously decreases the miscibility of the poly(hydroxybutyl methacrylate) and reduces the mobility in the mixt. to kinetically trap the phase sepn.  Carbonization of this polymer composite yields a porous nanocomposite.  This nanocomposite exhibits nearly three-fold greater gravimetric capacity in Na-ion batteries than the same titanium oxide nanoparticles that have been coated with carbon.  This improved performance is attributed to the morphol. as the carbon content in the composite is five times that of the coated nanoparticles.  The porous composite materials exhibit stable cyclic performance.  Moreover, the battery performance using materials from this polymn.-induced phase sepn. method is reproducible (capacity within 10% batch-to-batch).  This simple fabrication methodol. may be extendable to other systems and provides a facile route to generate reproducible hierarchical porous morphol. that can be beneficial in energy storage applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref38" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA04009D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hou, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jing, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jia, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhanced Sodium Storage Behavior of Carbon Coated Anatase TiO<sub>2</sub> Hollow Spheres</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">To inhibit the aggregation of TiO2 nanoparticles and to improve the electrochem. kinetics of TiO2 electrode, a hybrid material of ultra-small TiO2 nanoparticles in situ grown on rGO nanosheets was obtained by ultrasonic and reflux methods.  The size of the TiO2 particles was controlled ∼10 nm, and these particles were evenly distributed across the rGO nanosheets.  When used for the anode of a Na ion battery, the electrochem. performance of this hybrid TiO2@rGO was much improved.  A capacity of 186.6 mA h g-1 was obtained after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1, and 112.2 mA h g-1 could be maintained at 1.0 A g-1, showing a high capacity and good rate capability.  From the anal. of cyclic voltammetry (CV) and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS), the achieved excellent electrochem. performance was mainly attributed to the synergetic effect of well-dispersed ultra-small TiO2 nanoparticles and conductive graphene network and the improved electrochem. kinetics.  The superior electrochem. performance of this hybrid material on Li storage further confirmed the pos. effect of rGO.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref41" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.07.105"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ge, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qiu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Study on Structure and Electrochemical Sodiation of One-Dimensional Nanocrystalline TiO<sub>2</sub>@C Nanofiber Composites</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim. Acta</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">176</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">989</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">996</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2015.07.105</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D176%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D989-996%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DY.%2BGe%26author%3DJ.%2BZhu%26author%3DY.%2BLu%26author%3DC.%2BChen%26author%3DY.%2BQiu%26author%3DX.%2BZhang%26title%3DThe%2BStudy%2Bon%2BStructure%2Band%2BElectrochemical%2BSodiation%2Bof%2BOne-Dimensional%2BNanocrystalline%2BTiO2%2540C%2BNanofiber%2BComposites%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2015.07.105&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b03757&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2015.07.105&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The study on structure and electrochemical sodiation of one-dimensional nanocrystalline TiO2@C nanofiber composites</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ge, Yeqian; Zhu, Jiadeng; Lu, Yao; Chen, Chen; Qiu, Yiping; Zhang, Xiangwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">176</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">989-996</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">TiO2 (TiO2) is a prospective anode candidate for Na-ion batteries, owing to the advantages of good chem. stability, elemental abundance and nontoxicity.  TiO2 embedded in C nanofiber (TiO2@CNF) composites were prepd. for high-performance Na-ion batteries by electrospinning and subsequent heat treatment in N2 at different temps.  With increase in heat-treatment temp., the diam. of nanofibers decreases and the crystal phase partially transforms from anatase to rutile.  Among all composites, the TiO2@CNF composite treated at 550° has anatase structure and exhibits the highest initial reversible capacity (237.3 mAh g-1), largest initial coulombic efficiency (68.2%), and superior capacity retention (100.3%) over 100 cycles at 30 mA g-1.  Whereas, the TiO2@CNF composite treated at 650° is 28.23% rutile and 71.77% anatase, and shows the best rate capability of 159.1 mAh g-1 even at c.d. of 800 mA g-1.  It is, therefore, demonstrated that TiO2@CNF composites prepd. with appropriate conditions are superior anode material for Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref42" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1038/srep13862"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yeo, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jung, J.-W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, I.-D.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Graphene-Wrapped Anatase TiO<sub>2</sub> Nanofibers as High-Rate and Long-Cycle-Life Anode Material for Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Sci. Rep.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">5</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">13862</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/srep13862</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D13862%26journal%3DSci.%2BRep.%26author%3DY.%2BYeo%26author%3DJ.-W.%2BJung%26author%3DK.%2BPark%26author%3DI.-D.%2BKim%26title%3DGraphene-Wrapped%2BAnatase%2BTiO2%2BNanofibers%2Bas%2BHigh-Rate%2Band%2BLong-Cycle-Life%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1038%252Fsrep13862&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b03757&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fsrep13862&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Graphene-Wrapped Anatase TiO2 Nanofibers as High-Rate and Long-Cycle-Life Anode Material for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yeo Yeolmae; Jung Ji-Won; Kim Il-Doo; Park Kyusung</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scientific reports</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13862</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Anatase TiO2 has been suggested as a potential sodium anode material, but the low electrical conductivity of TiO2 often limits the rate capability, resulting in poor electrochemical properties.  To address this limitation, we propose graphene-wrapped anatase TiO2 nanofibers (rGO@TiO2 NFs) through an effective wrapping of reduced graphene oxide (rGO) sheets on electrospun TiO2 NFs.  To provide strong electrostatic interaction between the graphene oxide (GO) sheets and the TiO2 NFs, poly(allylamine hydrochloride) (PAH) was used to induce a positively charged TiO2 surface by the immobilization of the -NH3(+) group and to promote bonding with the negatively charged carboxylic acid (-COO(-)) and hydroxyl (-O(-)) groups on the GO.  A sodium anode electrode using rGO@TiO2 NFs exhibited a significantly improved initial capacity of 217 mAh g(-1), high capacity retention (85% after 200 cycles at 0.2C), and a high average Coulombic efficiency (99.7% from the second cycle to the 200th cycle), even at a 5C rate, compared to those of pristine TiO2 NFs.  The improved electrochemical performances stem from highly conductive properties of the reduced GO which is effectively anchored to the TiO2 NFs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref43" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1021/nl402747x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, K.-T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ali, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chung, K. Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yoon, C. S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yashiro, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, Y.-K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Amine, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Myung, S.-T.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Anatase Titania Nanorods as an Intercalation Anode Material for Rechargeable Sodium Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Lett.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">14</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">416</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">422</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/nl402747x</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D14%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D416-422%26journal%3DNano%2BLett.%26author%3DK.-T.%2BKim%26author%3DG.%2BAli%26author%3DK.%2BY.%2BChung%26author%3DC.%2BS.%2BYoon%26author%3DH.%2BYashiro%26author%3DY.-K.%2BSun%26author%3DJ.%2BLu%26author%3DK.%2BAmine%26author%3DS.-T.%2BMyung%26title%3DAnatase%2BTitania%2BNanorods%2Bas%2Ban%2BIntercalation%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BRechargeable%2BSodium%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fnl402747x&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b03757&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fnl402747x&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anatase Titania Nanorods as an Intercalation Anode Material for Rechargeable Sodium Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Ki-Tae; Ali, Ghulam; Chung, Kyung Yoon; Yoon, Chong Seung; Yashiro, Hitoshi; Sun, Yang-Kook; Lu, Jun; Amine, Khalil; Myung, Seung-Taek</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">416-422</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report the electrochem. activity of anatase TiO2 nanorods in a Na cell.  The anatase TiO2 nanorods were synthesized by a hydrothermal method, and their surfaces were coated by carbon to improve the elec. cond. by carbonization of pitch at 700° for 2 h in Ar flow.  The resulting structure does not change before and after the carbon coating, as confirmed by x-ray diffraction.  Transmission electron microscopy images confirm the presence of a carbon coating on the anatase TiO2 nanorods.  In cell tests, anodes of bare and carbon-coated anatase TiO2 nanorods exhibit stable cycling performance and attain a capacity of about 172 and 193 mA-h/g on the first charge, resp., in the voltage range of 0-3 V.  With the help of the conductive carbon layers, the carbon-coated anatase TiO2 delivers more capacity at high rates, 104 mA-h/g at the 10C rate (3.3 A/g), 82 mA-h/g at the 30C rate (10 A/g), and 53 mA-h/g at the 100C rate (33 A g-1).  By contrast, the anode of bare anatase TiO2 nanorods delivers only about 38 mA-h/g at the 10C rate (3.3 A/g).  The excellent cyclability and high-rate capability are the result of a Na+ insertion and extn. reaction into the host structure coupled with Ti4+/3+ redox reaction, as shown by x-ray absorption spectroscopy.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref44" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1021/jacs.5b04526"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, H.-W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhuo, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lin, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Artificial Solid Electrolyte Interphase-Protected Li<sub>x</sub>Si Nanoparticles: An Efficient and Stable Prelithiation Reagent for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Am. Chem. Soc.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">137</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">8372</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">8375</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/jacs.5b04526</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D137%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D8372-8375%26journal%3DJ.%2BAm.%2BChem.%2BSoc.%26author%3DJ.%2BZhao%26author%3DZ.%2BLu%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26author%3DW.%2BLiu%26author%3DH.-W.%2BLee%26author%3DK.%2BYan%26author%3DD.%2BZhuo%26author%3DD.%2BLin%26author%3DN.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BCui%26title%3DArtificial%2BSolid%2BElectrolyte%2BInterphase-Protected%2BLixSi%2BNanoparticles%253A%2BAn%2BEfficient%2Band%2BStable%2BPrelithiation%2BReagent%2Bfor%2BLithium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fjacs.5b04526&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b03757&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fjacs.5b04526&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Artificial solid electrolyte interphase-protected LixSi nanoparticles: an efficient and stable prelithiation reagent for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Jie; Lu, Zhenda; Wang, Haotian; Liu, Wei; Lee, Hyun-Wook; Yan, Kai; Zhuo, Denys; Lin, Dingchang; Liu, Nian; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">137</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">26</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8372-8375</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Prelithiation is an important strategy to compensate for lithium loss in lithium-ion batteries, particularly during the formation of the solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) from reduced electrolytes in the first charging cycle.  We recently demonstrated that LixSi nanoparticles (NPs) synthesized by thermal alloying can serve as a high-capacity prelithiation reagent, although their chem. stability in the battery processing environment remained to be improved.  Here we successfully developed a surface modification method to enhance the stability of LixSi NPs by exploiting the redn. of 1-fluorodecane on the LixSi surface to form a continuous and dense coating through a reaction process similar to SEI formation.  The coating, consisting of LiF and lithium alkyl carbonate with long hydrophobic carbon chains, serves as an effective passivation layer in the ambient environment.  Remarkably, artificial-SEI-protected LixSi NPs show a high prelithiation capacity of 2100 mA h g-1 with negligible capacity decay in dry air after 5 days and maintain a high capacity of 1600 mA h g-1 in humid air (∼10% relative humidity).  Silicon, tin, and graphite were successfully prelithiated with these NPs to eliminate the irreversible first-cycle capacity loss.  The use of prelithiation reagents offers a new approach to realize next-generation high-energy-d. lithium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="931886d84bb454b8-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32'],'ref33':['cit33'],'ref34':['cit34'],'ref35':['cit35'],'ref36':['cit36'],'ref37':['cit37'],'ref38':['cit38'],'ref39':['cit39'],'ref40':['cit40'],'ref41':['cit41'],'ref42':['cit42'],'ref43':['cit43'],'ref44':['cit44']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries have attracted great attention particularly in large-scale elec. energy storage applications for renewable energy and smart grid because of the huge abundant sodium resources and low cost.  In this article, a variety of electrode materials including cathodes and anodes as well as electrolytes for room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries are briefly reviewed.  We compare the difference in storage behavior between Na and Li in their analogous electrodes and summarize the sodium storage mechanisms in the available electrode materials.  This review also includes some new results from our group and our thoughts on developing new materials.  Some perspectives and directions on designing better materials for practical applications are pointed out based on knowledge from the literature and our experience.  Through this extensive literature review, the search for suitable electrode and electrolyte materials for stationary sodium-ion batteries is still challenging.  However, after intensive research efforts, we believe that low-cost, long-life and room-temp. sodium-ion batteries would be promising for applications in large-scale energy storage system in the near future.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1039/c2ee02781j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Palomares, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Serras, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Villaluenga, I.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hueso, K.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1039/C4EE03192J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, M.                         rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A comprehensive review of sodium layered oxides: powerful cathodes for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Han, Man Huon; Gonzalo, Elena; Singh, Gurpreet; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The room temp. Na-ion secondary battery has been under focus lately due to its feasibility to compete against the already well-established Li-ion secondary battery.  Although there are many obstacles to overcome before the Na-ion battery becomes com. available, recent research discoveries corroborate that some of the cathode materials for the Na-ion battery have indeed indisputable advantages over its Li-ion counterparts.  In this publication, a comprehensive review of layered oxides (NaTMO2, TM = Ti, V, Cr, Mn, Fe, Co, Ni, and a mixt. of 2 or 3 elements) as a viable Na-ion battery cathode is presented.  Single TM systems are well characterized not only for their electrochem. performance but also for their structural transitions during the cycle.  Binary TM systems are investigated in order to address issues regarding low reversible capacity, capacity retention, operating voltage, and structural stability.  As a consequence, some materials already have reached an energy d. of 520 mW h g-1, which is comparable to that of LiFePO4.  Furthermore, some ternary TM systems retained more than 72% of their capacity along with over 99.7% Coulombic efficiency for 275 cycles.  The goal of this review is to present the development of Na layered oxide materials in the past as well as the state of the art today in order to emphasize the compatibility and durability of layered oxides as powerful candidates for Na-ion battery cathode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201501727"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Deng, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Routes to High Energy Cathodes of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv. Commun.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">6</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">6954</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/ncomms7954</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">P2-Na0.6[Cr0.6Ti0.4]O2 cation-disordered electrode for high-rate symmetric rechargeable sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Yuesheng; Xiao, Ruijuan; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Avdeev, Maxim; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6954</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2041-1723</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Most P2-type layered oxides exhibit Na+/vacancy-ordered superstructures because of strong Na+-Na+ interaction in the alkali metal layer and charge ordering in the transition metal layer.  These superstructures evidenced by voltage plateaus in the electrochem. curves limit the Na+ ion transport kinetics and cycle performance in rechargeable batteries.  Here we show that such Na+/vacancy ordering can be avoided by choosing the transition metal ions with similar ionic radii and different redox potentials, for example, Cr3+ and Ti4+.  The designed P2-Na0.6[Cr0.6Ti0.4]O2 is completely Na+/vacancy-disordered at any sodium content and displays excellent rate capability and long cycle life.  A sym. sodium-ion battery using the same P2-Na0.6[Cr0.6Ti0.4]O2 electrode delivers 75% of the initial capacity at 12C rate.  Our contribution demonstrates that the approach of preventing Na+/vacancy ordering by breaking charge ordering in the transition metal layer opens a simple way to design disordered electrode materials with high power d. and long cycle life.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1039/C5EE01365H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Talaie, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Duffort, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Smith, H.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A combination of operando X-ray diffraction, pair distribution function (PDF) anal. coupled with electrochem. measurements and M.ovrddot.ossbauer spectroscopy elucidates the nature of the phase transitions induced by insertion and extn. of sodium ions in P2-Na0.67[NiyMn0.5+yFe0.5-2y]O2 (y = 0, 0.10, 0.15). The crystal structure of the high voltage phase is solved for the first time by X-ray PDF anal. of P2-Na0.67-zFe0.5Mn0.5O2 (where z ∼ 0.5), revealing that migration of the transition metals - particularly Fe3+ - into tetrahedral sites in the interlayer space occurs at high potential.  This results in new short range order between two adjacent layers.  Although the transition metal migration is reversible as proven by electrochem. performance, it induces a large disfavorable cell polarization.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have attracted extensive interest for energy storage and conversion as an alternative to lithium-ion batteries.  The development of advanced electrode materials is important for the implementation of sodium-ion batteries into practical applications.  Herein, we developed a facile soaking-chem. vapor deposition method to grow core-sheath structured Sn@CNT nanopillar arrays on carbon paper with a unique 3D hierarchical architecture as free-standing electrode for sodium-ion batteries.  The electrode achieved a reversible capacity of 887 μA h cm-2 in the first cycle and good cyclability extending to 100 cycles.  The electrode also demonstrated a promising rate capability, which is suitable for high power applications.  We also assembled prototype Na-ion full cells, consisting of the as-prepd. free-standing Sn@CNT@carbon paper anode and Na0.80Li0.12Ni0.22Mn0.66O2 cathode.  The full sodium-ion battery can power LED lights.  This work is expected to inspire the development of sustainable sodium-ion batteries for energy storage and conversion.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref16" class="rightTabRefNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit16" data-doi="10.1039/C3EE42944J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pei, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mao, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ai, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sb-C Nanofibers with Long Cycle Life as An Anode Material for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Stannous sulfide@reduced graphene oxide (SnS@RGO) composite is successfully synthesized via a facile pptn. route.  The structural and morphol. characterizations reveal SnS@RGO composites are composed of SnS nanoparticles of the size 5-10 nm, which are uniformly anchored on the surface of RGO.  The electrochem. measurements demonstrate the reversible capacity of the SnS@RGO composite - that includes contributions from the conversion reaction of SnS to Sn and NaxS and the alloying reaction of Sn to NaxSn.  The SnS@RGO electrode exhibits a reversible capacity of 457 mA h g-1 at 20 mA g-1, superior cycling stability (94% capacity retention over 100 cycles at 100 mA g-1) and adequate rate performance.  Compared to the neat SnS nanoparticles, the enhanced electrochem. performance of the SnS@RGO composite is primarily due to the incorporation of RGO as a highly conductive, flexible component as well as possessing a large available surface area, which provides desirable properties such as improved electronic contact between active materials, aggregation suppression of intermediate products, and alleviation of the vol. change during sodiation and desodiation. In this paper, a green approach is described for the synthesis of Sn4P3/C nanocomposite and demonstrated its excellent Na-storage performance as a novel anode of Na-ion batteries.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb is a promising high-capacity anode material in Na-ion batteries, but it generally shows poor cycling stability because of its large vol. changes during Na ion insertion and extn. processes.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Well-organized C nanotube (CNT)@TiO2 core/porous-sheath coaxial nanocables were synthesized by controlled hydrolysis of tetra-Bu titanate in the presence of CNTs - these were studied with SEM, TEM, XRD and electrochem. expts.  The CNT@TiO2 coaxial nanocables show excellent rate capability and cycling performance compared with both pure CNT and pure TiO2 when used as anode materials for Li-ion batteries (LIBs).  Both the sp. capacity in the CNT core and that in the TiO2 sheath are much higher than that of the TiO2-free CNT and that of the CNT-free TiO2 sample, resp.  The coaxial cable morphol. provides a soln. to the ionic-electronic wiring problem in LIBs as well as the synergism of the 2 cable wall materials.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are an attractive alternative to lithium-ion batteries that alleviate problems with lithium availability and cost.  Despite several studies of cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries involving layered oxide materials, there are few low-voltage metal oxide anodes capable of operating sodium ion reversibly at room temp.  We have synthesized amorphous titanium dioxide nanotube electrodes directly grown on current collectors without binders and additives to use as an anode for sodium-ion batteries.  We find that only amorphous large diam. nanotubes (&gt;80 nm I.D.) can support electrochem. cycling with sodium ions.  These electrodes maximize their capacity in operando and reach reversible capacity of 150 mA-h/g in 15 cycles. The TiO2 NTAs on Ti foam were used as anodes in lithium ion batteries; they exhibited high capacities of 103 μAh cm-2 at 10 μA cm-2 and 83 μAh cm-2 at 500 μA cm-2, which are two to three times higher than those achieved on the std. In addn., a Na-ion half-cell composed of these NTAs anodes and Na metal as the counter electrode showed a self-improved specific capacity upon cycling at 10 μA cm-2.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered to be a promising low-cost alternative to common lithium-ion batteries.  Herein, we present a detailed electrochem. characterization of anatase TiO2 nanoparticles as anode material for Na-ion batteries, highlighting the substantial influence of the electrolyte compn. (salt and solvent) on the obtainable specific capacity, cycling stability, and particularly the coulombic efficiency.  TiO2-based electrodes cycled using a 1M soln. of NaClO4 in a mixt. of ethylene carbonate and propylene carbonate present excellent high rate capability, offering about 100 and 86 mAh g-1 at 5.5 and 11 C, resp., which is - to the best of our knowledge - the best high rate capability for all titanium-based sodium-ion anode materials reported so far.  Setting the C rate to 5.5C (i.e., 1.85 A g-1), such electrodes can be cycled for more than 1000 cycles without significant capacity decay, confirming their outstanding durability at such high specific current.  These results, in combination with its environmental friendliness and cost efficiency, render anatase TiO2 nanoparticles a promising anode material for high power sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA00614G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jia, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Anatase TiO<sub>2</sub> Nanocubes for Fast and Durable Sodium Ion Battery Anodes</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">With the aim of advancing anatase TiO2 anodes for Na ion batteries, cryst. TiO2 nanocubes were employed and they delivered a gradually increasing capacity during the initial cycles, termed as an activation process.  The no. of necessary discharge-charge loops for total activation is dependent on the galvanostatic c.d. (∼20 cycles at 0.2 C, or 90 cycles at 1 C).  A percentage of Ti3+ was detected after the activation, indicating an amt. of irreversibly trapped Na ions in the lattice.  After the activation process, an excellent rate capability and outstanding cycling stability were presented.  The reversible capacity reached 174, 132, and 108 mA h g-1 at rates of 1 C, 5 C, and 10 C, resp.  The capacity was sustained with a loss of &lt;10% after 1000 discharge-charge cycles at a rate of 2 C or 10 C.  The superior battery performance achieved by the nanocubes is related to the encircled {100} facets that are more favorable for Na ion attachment compared to the {001} and {101} facets, as supported by 1st-principles calcns.  From this work the authors can see the feasibility of optimizing electrode materials via rational surface structure construction based on theor. calcns.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref30" class="rightTabRefNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit30" data-doi="10.1039/C5CP01227A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hou, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jing, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An Electrochemical Investigation of Rutile TiO<sub>2</sub> Microspheres Anchored by Nanoneedle Clusters for Sodium Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Phys.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Rutile TiO2 microspheres anchored by nanoneedle clusters, as a new class of anode materials, are successfully employed for sodium-ion batteries and manifested good energy storage behavior.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Exploring new anode materials is important for developing sodium ion batteries.  In this work, TiO2(B) nanotubes are prepd. by hydrothermal reaction in concd. NaOH soln. and subsequent calcination at 300 °C in air, and investigated for the first time as anodes for sodium ion batteries.  It is demonstrated that TiO2(B) nanotubes are several hundred nanometers in length with an outer diam. of about 10-15 nm.  Moreover, the interference fringe spacings of the nanotubes are derived from the TEM image, being about 0.56 and 0.34 nm, which are consistent with the interplanar distances of the (001) and (110) planes in the TiO2(B) phase, resp.  As anticipated, the interlayer spacing of the (001) plane in the TiO2(B) nanotubes is large enough to accommodate sodium ions.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. properties of TiO2 with the hollandite structure (TiO2(H)) as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries are reported.  TiO2(H) was obtained from hollandite K0.21TiO2 by an oxidn.-ion extn. process.  Na/TiO2(H) cells exhibit a large first discharge capacity of 280 mA-h/g down to 0.2 V.  After the first discharge the Na/TiO2(H) cells develop a reversible charge-discharge capacity of 85 mA-h/g at C/8 rate in the 2.5-0.2 V voltage range; this corresponds to the reversible insertion of 0.25 Na per TiO2(H) formula unit.  Chronoamperometry and potentiostatic intermittent titrn. techniques were used to further characterize the electrochem. reaction mechanism.  Structural changes in the TiO2(H) electrode upon sodium insertion and extn. have been studied by ex situ x-ray diffraction (XRD) and high resoln. in situ synchrotron diffraction techniques, for which appropriately modified coin-type cells were used.  It is seen that sodium insertion into TiO2(H) is commenced with a single-phase solid soln. followed by a structural transition from tetragonal I4/m to monoclinic I2/m symmetry, in which the skeleton framework is retained.  The reversible transition includes few structural changes with a small vol. change of only 1.1%.  Fourier difference maps deduced from SXRD patterns revealed the location of Na ions in 4i sites in the tunnel space.  The coordination arrangement around Na ions is distorted capped trigonal prisms formed by seven oxygen atoms.  Although still far from the theor. capacity (335 mA-h/g), the cycling properties at a low insertion potential together with the host framework stability indicate the feasibility of TiO2 with the hollandite structure as an anode material for Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref35" class="rightTabRefNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit35" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b02348"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Su, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dou, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Anatase TiO<sub>2</sub>: Better Anode Material Than Amorphous and Rutile Phases of TiO<sub>2</sub> for Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Polymn.-induced phase sepn. of nanoparticle-filled soln. is demonstrated as a simple approach to control the structure of porous composites.  These composites are subsequently demonstrated as the active component for sodium-ion battery anode.  To synthesize the composites, we dissolved/dispersed titanium oxide (anatase) nanoparticles (for sodium insertion) and poly(hydroxybutyl methacrylate) (porogen) in furfuryl alc. (carbon precursor) contg. a photoacid generator.  UV exposure converts the photoacid generator to a strong acid that catalyzes the furfuryl alc. polymn.  This polymn. simultaneously decreases the miscibility of the poly(hydroxybutyl methacrylate) and reduces the mobility in the mixt. to kinetically trap the phase sepn.  Carbonization of this polymer composite yields a porous nanocomposite.  This nanocomposite exhibits nearly three-fold greater gravimetric capacity in Na-ion batteries than the same titanium oxide nanoparticles that have been coated with carbon.  This improved performance is attributed to the morphol. as the carbon content in the composite is five times that of the coated nanoparticles.  The porous composite materials exhibit stable cyclic performance.  Moreover, the battery performance using materials from this polymn.-induced phase sepn. method is reproducible (capacity within 10% batch-to-batch).  This simple fabrication methodol. may be extendable to other systems and provides a facile route to generate reproducible hierarchical porous morphol. that can be beneficial in energy storage applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref38" class="rightTabRefNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit38" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA04009D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hou, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jing, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jia, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhanced Sodium Storage Behavior of Carbon Coated Anatase TiO<sub>2</sub> Hollow Spheres</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are emerging as a highly promising technol. for large-scale energy storage applications.  However, it remains a significant challenge to develop an anode with superior long-term cycling stability and high-rate capability.  Here we demonstrate that the Na+ intercalation pseudocapacitance in TiO2/graphene nanocomposites enables high-rate capability and long cycle life in a sodium-ion battery.  This hybrid electrode exhibits a specific capacity of above 90 mA h g-1 at 12,000 mA g-1 (∼36 C).  The capacity is highly reversible for more than 4,000 cycles, the longest demonstrated cyclability to date.  First-principle calcns. demonstrate that the intimate integration of graphene with TiO2 reduces the diffusion energy barrier, thus enhancing the Na+ intercalation pseudocapacitive process.  The Na-ion intercalation pseudocapacitance enabled by tailor-deigned nanostructures represents a promising strategy for developing electrode materials with high power d. and long cycle life.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref40" class="rightTabRefNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit40" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b02724"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yuan, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrasmall TiO<sub>2</sub> Nanoparticles in Situ Growth on Graphene Hybrid as Superior Anode Material for Sodium/Lithium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">7</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">11239</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">11245</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.5b02724</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrasmall TiO2 Nanoparticles in Situ Growth on Graphene Hybrid as Superior Anode Material for Sodium/Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Huiqiao; Cao, Kangzhe; Xu, Xiaohong; Jiao, Lifang; Wang, Yijing; Yuan, Huatang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11239-11245</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">To inhibit the aggregation of TiO2 nanoparticles and to improve the electrochem. kinetics of TiO2 electrode, a hybrid material of ultra-small TiO2 nanoparticles in situ grown on rGO nanosheets was obtained by ultrasonic and reflux methods.  The size of the TiO2 particles was controlled ∼10 nm, and these particles were evenly distributed across the rGO nanosheets.  When used for the anode of a Na ion battery, the electrochem. performance of this hybrid TiO2@rGO was much improved.  A capacity of 186.6 mA h g-1 was obtained after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1, and 112.2 mA h g-1 could be maintained at 1.0 A g-1, showing a high capacity and good rate capability.  From the anal. of cyclic voltammetry (CV) and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS), the achieved excellent electrochem. performance was mainly attributed to the synergetic effect of well-dispersed ultra-small TiO2 nanoparticles and conductive graphene network and the improved electrochem. kinetics.  The superior electrochem. performance of this hybrid material on Li storage further confirmed the pos. effect of rGO.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref41" class="rightTabRefNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit41" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.07.105"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ge, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qiu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Study on Structure and Electrochemical Sodiation of One-Dimensional Nanocrystalline TiO<sub>2</sub>@C Nanofiber Composites</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim. Acta</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">176</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">989</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">996</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2015.07.105</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The study on structure and electrochemical sodiation of one-dimensional nanocrystalline TiO2@C nanofiber composites</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ge, Yeqian; Zhu, Jiadeng; Lu, Yao; Chen, Chen; Qiu, Yiping; Zhang, Xiangwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">176</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">989-996</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">TiO2 (TiO2) is a prospective anode candidate for Na-ion batteries, owing to the advantages of good chem. stability, elemental abundance and nontoxicity.  TiO2 embedded in C nanofiber (TiO2@CNF) composites were prepd. for high-performance Na-ion batteries by electrospinning and subsequent heat treatment in N2 at different temps.  With increase in heat-treatment temp., the diam. of nanofibers decreases and the crystal phase partially transforms from anatase to rutile.  Among all composites, the TiO2@CNF composite treated at 550° has anatase structure and exhibits the highest initial reversible capacity (237.3 mAh g-1), largest initial coulombic efficiency (68.2%), and superior capacity retention (100.3%) over 100 cycles at 30 mA g-1.  Whereas, the TiO2@CNF composite treated at 650° is 28.23% rutile and 71.77% anatase, and shows the best rate capability of 159.1 mAh g-1 even at c.d. of 800 mA g-1.  It is, therefore, demonstrated that TiO2@CNF composites prepd. with appropriate conditions are superior anode material for Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref42" class="rightTabRefNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit42" data-doi="10.1038/srep13862"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yeo, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jung, J.-W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, I.-D.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Graphene-Wrapped Anatase TiO<sub>2</sub> Nanofibers as High-Rate and Long-Cycle-Life Anode Material for Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Sci. Rep.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">5</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">13862</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/srep13862</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Graphene-Wrapped Anatase TiO2 Nanofibers as High-Rate and Long-Cycle-Life Anode Material for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yeo Yeolmae; Jung Ji-Won; Kim Il-Doo; Park Kyusung</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scientific reports</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13862</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Anatase TiO2 has been suggested as a potential sodium anode material, but the low electrical conductivity of TiO2 often limits the rate capability, resulting in poor electrochemical properties.  To address this limitation, we propose graphene-wrapped anatase TiO2 nanofibers (rGO@TiO2 NFs) through an effective wrapping of reduced graphene oxide (rGO) sheets on electrospun TiO2 NFs.  To provide strong electrostatic interaction between the graphene oxide (GO) sheets and the TiO2 NFs, poly(allylamine hydrochloride) (PAH) was used to induce a positively charged TiO2 surface by the immobilization of the -NH3(+) group and to promote bonding with the negatively charged carboxylic acid (-COO(-)) and hydroxyl (-O(-)) groups on the GO.  A sodium anode electrode using rGO@TiO2 NFs exhibited a significantly improved initial capacity of 217 mAh g(-1), high capacity retention (85% after 200 cycles at 0.2C), and a high average Coulombic efficiency (99.7% from the second cycle to the 200th cycle), even at a 5C rate, compared to those of pristine TiO2 NFs.  The improved electrochemical performances stem from highly conductive properties of the reduced GO which is effectively anchored to the TiO2 NFs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref43" class="rightTabRefNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit43" data-doi="10.1021/nl402747x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, K.-T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ali, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chung, K. Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yoon, C. S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yashiro, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, Y.-K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Amine, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Myung, S.-T.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Anatase Titania Nanorods as an Intercalation Anode Material for Rechargeable Sodium Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Lett.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">14</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">416</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">422</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/nl402747x</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anatase Titania Nanorods as an Intercalation Anode Material for Rechargeable Sodium Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Ki-Tae; Ali, Ghulam; Chung, Kyung Yoon; Yoon, Chong Seung; Yashiro, Hitoshi; Sun, Yang-Kook; Lu, Jun; Amine, Khalil; Myung, Seung-Taek</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">416-422</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report the electrochem. activity of anatase TiO2 nanorods in a Na cell.  The anatase TiO2 nanorods were synthesized by a hydrothermal method, and their surfaces were coated by carbon to improve the elec. cond. by carbonization of pitch at 700° for 2 h in Ar flow.  The resulting structure does not change before and after the carbon coating, as confirmed by x-ray diffraction.  Transmission electron microscopy images confirm the presence of a carbon coating on the anatase TiO2 nanorods.  In cell tests, anodes of bare and carbon-coated anatase TiO2 nanorods exhibit stable cycling performance and attain a capacity of about 172 and 193 mA-h/g on the first charge, resp., in the voltage range of 0-3 V.  With the help of the conductive carbon layers, the carbon-coated anatase TiO2 delivers more capacity at high rates, 104 mA-h/g at the 10C rate (3.3 A/g), 82 mA-h/g at the 30C rate (10 A/g), and 53 mA-h/g at the 100C rate (33 A g-1).  By contrast, the anode of bare anatase TiO2 nanorods delivers only about 38 mA-h/g at the 10C rate (3.3 A/g).  The excellent cyclability and high-rate capability are the result of a Na+ insertion and extn. reaction into the host structure coupled with Ti4+/3+ redox reaction, as shown by x-ray absorption spectroscopy.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref44" class="rightTabRefNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit44" data-doi="10.1021/jacs.5b04526"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, H.-W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhuo, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lin, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Artificial Solid Electrolyte Interphase-Protected Li<sub>x</sub>Si Nanoparticles: An Efficient and Stable Prelithiation Reagent for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Am. Chem. Soc.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">137</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">8372</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">8375</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/jacs.5b04526</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Artificial solid electrolyte interphase-protected LixSi nanoparticles: an efficient and stable prelithiation reagent for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Jie; Lu, Zhenda; Wang, Haotian; Liu, Wei; Lee, Hyun-Wook; Yan, Kai; Zhuo, Denys; Lin, Dingchang; Liu, Nian; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">137</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">26</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8372-8375</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Prelithiation is an important strategy to compensate for lithium loss in lithium-ion batteries, particularly during the formation of the solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) from reduced electrolytes in the first charging cycle.  We recently demonstrated that LixSi nanoparticles (NPs) synthesized by thermal alloying can serve as a high-capacity prelithiation reagent, although their chem. stability in the battery processing environment remained to be improved.  Here we successfully developed a surface modification method to enhance the stability of LixSi NPs by exploiting the redn. of 1-fluorodecane on the LixSi surface to form a continuous and dense coating through a reaction process similar to SEI formation.  The coating, consisting of LiF and lithium alkyl carbonate with long hydrophobic carbon chains, serves as an effective passivation layer in the ambient environment.  Remarkably, artificial-SEI-protected LixSi NPs show a high prelithiation capacity of 2100 mA h g-1 with negligible capacity decay in dry air after 5 days and maintain a high capacity of 1600 mA h g-1 in humid air (∼10% relative humidity).  Silicon, tin, and graphite were successfully prelithiated with these NPs to eliminate the irreversible first-cycle capacity loss.  The use of prelithiation reagents offers a new approach to realize next-generation high-energy-d. lithium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i8">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsami.6b03757" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsami.6b03757</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Schematic illustration of the preparation process for the TiO<sub>2</sub>/C nanofibers, EDX element mapping characterization of the TiO<sub>2</sub>/C nanofibers, Na-storage capacities of the carbon fibers and conductive super P carbon powder, morphological characterization of the TiO<sub>2</sub>/C nanofibers after cycling, and charge/discharge performance of the TiO<sub>2</sub>/Na<sub>2</sub>FeFe(CN)<sub>6</sub> full cell (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.6b03757/suppl_file/am6b03757_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.6b03757/suppl_file/am6b03757_si_001.pdf">am6b03757_si_001.pdf (2.45 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">
